Investing in AI Amid Geopolitical and Supply Risks

Bloomberg Television(3.1M) ·10:38 ·2.2K views · 2026-04-21
Winston Cheng (CFO, Lenovo) Helen Zhu (NF Trinity)
The AI revolution remains in its "early innings" with massive demand for infrastructure and devices outstripping supply.
TL;DR The AI revolution remains in its "early innings" with massive demand for infrastructure and devices outstripping supply. While extreme memory price hikes and geopolitical tensions pose risks, major players are mitigating these through global supply chain diversification...

TL;DR

The AI revolution remains in its "early innings" with massive demand for infrastructure and devices outstripping supply. While extreme memory price hikes and geopolitical tensions pose risks, major players are mitigating these through global supply chain diversification and a strategic focus on "picks and shovels" infrastructure.

Market Dynamics and AI Adoption

  • Early Stages of Growth: Both speakers emphasize that the AI cycle is in its infancy. Winston Cheng notes strong demand across both device (PC) and infrastructure (server) segments.
  • Enterprise Experimentation: Helen Zhu highlights that enterprise-level AI is in the "super early" experimental phase, involving APIs and tools like Claude, with significant room for scale.
  • Device Market Stability: Despite potential price hikes, the global PC market remains resilient.
      • Demand Floor: The market historically holds at roughly 270 million units annually.
      • AI Integration: Substantial future demand is expected as users require local compute power to interact with AI models effectively.
  • Speed of Innovation: Software disruption is occurring faster than predicted. "Agentic commerce" (end-to-end AI transactions), which many experts thought was years away, is already becoming commonplace.

Supply Chain Realities and Geopolitical Risks

  • Memory Crunch: Component costs have surged, with memory prices reportedly increasing 400–500% in the final quarter of last year.
  • Geopolitical Impact:
      • Regional vs. Global: Conflict in the Middle East has affected regional shipments but has not yet disrupted global supply chains.
      • Diversification: Lenovo is mitigating "China-related risk" and tariffs by building manufacturing plants close to demand centers, including Riyadh (for the METEA region), Mexico, Europe, and North America.
  • Market Consolidation: A "volume of delivery" issue exists. Larger players with established supply chain support are successfully grabbing limited resources, leading to market share consolidation.
  • CapEx Trends: Hyperscalers are currently spending close to 100% of their annual cash flow on Capital Expenditure (CapEx) to build out AI capacity.

Corporate Strategy and Capital Allocation

  • Infrastructure Pivot: Lenovo is aggressively deploying capital into its Infrastructure Solutions Group (ISG), moving beyond its traditional PC-centric model to support the "picks and shovels" of the AI era.
  • Margin Management:
      • Server/ISG Side: Due to the demand-supply imbalance, manufacturers currently have the leverage to pass component cost increases through to customers.
      • Device Side: Companies remain cautious about passing costs to consumers, as price elasticity in the PC market is more sensitive.
  • Strategic Partnerships: Lenovo is leveraging its scale to form technology and supply partnerships with emerging ecosystem players like Nscale to ensure alignment in the server space.

The Investment "Roadmap"

  • The "Sure Bet": NF Trinity’s Helen Zhu suggests the most reliable investment strategy currently lies in infrastructure—the "picks and shovels"—which continues to see upward earnings revisions.
  • Avoiding the Disrupted: Investors are increasingly wary of companies that could be "AI-disrupted" over the medium term. Zhu warns against playing these companies for "small bounces" and suggests pivoting toward potential winners in the infrastructure stack.
  • Software Vulnerability: Native AI applications that were considered "front-runners" only a year ago are already being disrupted as Large Language Models (LLMs) move directly into specific industry verticals.

Notable Quotes

"Particularly on the infrastructure side, we're seeing that as long as you supply, you will have the demand." — Winston Cheng
"Right now I think it's really the picks and shovels and the infrastructure that's continuously getting upward revisions and that's probably the most sure bet in terms of this AI trade." — Helen Zhu
"Hyperscalers [are] spending now a lot portion of their cash flow... getting close to 100 percent of the annual cash flow on CapEx." — Winston Cheng
"I think the hallucination is getting much much better... I use AI now on a daily basis versus in the past [when] you are maybe at best weekly." — Winston Cheng
